(June 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Trinidad is also notable for containing <a href="/wiki/Pitch_Lake" title="Pitch Lake">Pitch Lake</a>, the largest natural reservoir of <a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">asphalt</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> Tobago contains a flat plain in its south-west, with the eastern half of the island being more mountainous, culminating in Pigeon Peak, the island's highest point at 550 metres (1,800&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Anthony_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anthony-101">[97]</a></sup> Tobago also contains several coral reefs off its coast.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The majority of the population reside on the island of Trinidad, and this is thus the location of largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="List of cities and towns in Trinidad and Tobago">towns and cities</a>. There are four major municipalities in Trinidad: the capital Port of Spain, <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="San Fernando, Trinidad and Tobago">San Fernando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arima" title="Arima">Arima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chaguanas" title="Chaguanas">Chaguanas</a>. The main town on Tobago is <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_Tobago" title="Scarborough, Tobago">Scarborough</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trinidad#Geology" title="Trinidad">Trinidad §&nbsp;Geology</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Northern Range consists mainly of Upper Jurassic and <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> <a href="/wiki/Metamorphic_rock" title="Metamorphic rock">metamorphic rocks</a>. The Northern Lowlands (the East–West Corridor and <a href="/wiki/Caroni_Plain" title="Caroni Plain">Caroni Plain</a>) consist of younger shallow marine <a href="/wiki/Clastic_sediment" class="mw-redirect" title="Clastic sediment">clastic sediments</a>. South of this, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Range,_Trinidad" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Range, Trinidad">Central Range</a> <a href="/wiki/Fold_and_thrust_belt" title="Fold and thrust belt">fold and thrust belt</a> consists of Cretaceous and <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> formations along the southern and eastern flanks. The <a href="/wiki/Naparima_Plain" title="Naparima Plain">Naparima Plain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nariva_Swamp" title="Nariva Swamp">Nariva Swamp</a> form the southern shoulder of this uplift.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Southern Lowlands consist of Miocene and <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> sands, clays, and gravels. These overlie oil and natural gas deposits, especially north of the Los Bajos Fault. The Southern Range forms the third <a href="/wiki/Anticline" title="Anticline">anticlinal</a> uplift. The rocks consist of <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">shales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siltstone" title="Siltstone">siltstones</a> and clays formed in the Miocene and uplifted in the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tar_sands" class="mw-redirect" title="Tar sands">Oil sands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mud_volcano" title="Mud volcano">mud volcanoes</a> are especially common in this area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg/220px-STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg/330px-STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg/440px-STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2178"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:STAPP_114_La_Brea_Pitch_Lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Pitch Lake, in south-west Trinidad
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago has a maritime <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> There are two seasons annually: the <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> for the first five months of the year, and the <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season">rainy season</a> in the remaining seven of the year. Winds are predominantly from the northeast and are dominated by the northeast <a href="/wiki/Trade_wind" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade wind">trade winds</a>. Unlike many Caribbean islands Trinidad and Tobago lies outside the main hurricane alleys; nevertheless, the island of Tobago was struck by Hurricane Flora on 30 September 1963. In the Northern Range of Trinidad, the climate is often cooler than that of the sweltering heat of the plains below, due to constant cloud and mist cover, and heavy rains in the mountains. </p>
      <p>Record temperatures for Trinidad and Tobago are 39&nbsp;°C (102&nbsp;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup> for the high in Port of Spain, and a low of 12&nbsp;°C (54&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Environment of Trinidad and Tobago">Environment of Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mayaro_Beach;_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg/220px-Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg/330px-Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg/440px-Mayaro_Beach%3B_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mayaro_Beach;_Trinidad_%26_Tobago.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mayaro,_Trinidad" title="Mayaro, Trinidad">Mayaro</a> Beach, in the southeastern area of Trinidad
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Because Trinidad and Tobago lies on the continental shelf of South America, and in ancient times were physically connected to the South American mainland, its biological diversity is unlike that of most other Caribbean islands, and has much more in common with that of Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018270_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018270-104">[100]</a></sup> The main ecosystems are: coastal and marine (coral reefs, mangrove swamps, open ocean and seagrass beds); forest; freshwater (rivers and streams); <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a>; man-made ecosystems (agricultural land, freshwater dams, secondary forest); and savanna. On 1 August 1996, Trinidad and Tobago ratified the 1992 Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a>, and it has produced a biodiversity action plan and four reports describing the country's contribution to biodiversity conservation. These reports formally acknowledged the importance of biodiversity to the well-being of the country's people through provision of <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem_service" title="Ecosystem service">ecosystem services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar,_USVI_(5839996547).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg/220px-Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg/330px-Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg/440px-Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar%2C_USVI_%285839996547%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1864" data-file-height="1085"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Leatherback_sea_turtle_Tinglar,_USVI_(5839996547).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Trinidad and Tobago is a major nesting site for <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">Leatherback Turtles</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Information about vertebrates is good, with 472 bird species (2 endemics), about 100 mammals, about 90 reptiles (a few endemics), about 30 amphibians (including several endemics), 50 freshwater fish and at least 950 marine fish.<sup id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-106">[102]</a></sup> Notable mammal species include the <a href="/wiki/Ocelot" title="Ocelot">ocelot</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_manatee" title="West Indian manatee">West Indian manatee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collared_peccary" title="Collared peccary">collared peccary</a> (known as the quenk locally), <a href="/wiki/Red-rumped_agouti" title="Red-rumped agouti">red-rumped agouti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lowland_paca" title="Lowland paca">lappe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_brocket" title="Red brocket">red brocket deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neotropical_otter" title="Neotropical otter">Neotropical otter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wedge-capped_capuchin" title="Wedge-capped capuchin">weeper capuchin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyanan_red_howler" title="Guyanan red howler">red howler monkey</a>; there are also some 70 species of <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bat</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Vampire_bat" title="Vampire bat">vampire bat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fringe-lipped_bat" title="Fringe-lipped bat">fringe-lipped bat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018273_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018273-107">[103]</a></sup> The larger reptiles present include 5 species of marine turtles known to nest on the islands' beaches, the <a href="/wiki/Green_anaconda" title="Green anaconda">green anaconda</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Boa_constrictor" title="Boa constrictor">Boa constrictor</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Spectacled_caiman" title="Spectacled caiman">spectacled caiman</a>. There are at least 47 species of snakes, including only four dangerous venomous species (only in Trinidad and not in Tobago), lizards such as the <a href="/wiki/Green_iguana" title="Green iguana">green iguana</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tupinambis_cryptus" title="Tupinambis cryptus">Tupinambis cryptus</a> and a few species of fresh water turtles and land tortoises.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018274_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018274-108">[104]</a></sup> are present. Of the amphibians, the <a href="/wiki/Common_tree_frog" title="Common tree frog">golden tree frog</a> is found only in the highest peaks of Trinidad's Northern Range and nearby in those of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>'s Paria Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018274_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018274-108">[104]</a></sup> Marine life is abundant, with several species of <a href="/wiki/Sea_urchin" title="Sea urchin">sea urchin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anemone" title="Anemone">anemone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starfish" title="Starfish">starfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manta_ray" title="Manta ray">manta ray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porpoise" title="Porpoise">porpoise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whale_shark" title="Whale shark">whale shark</a> present in the islands' waters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018276_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018276-109">[105]</a></sup> The introduced <a href="/wiki/Pterois" title="Pterois">Pterois</a> is viewed as a pest, as it eats many native species of fish and has no natural predators; efforts are currently underway to cull the numbers of this species.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018276_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018276-109">[105]</a></sup> The country contains five terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_moist_forests" title="Trinidad and Tobago moist forests">Trinidad and Tobago moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antillean_dry_forests" title="Lesser Antillean dry forests">Lesser Antillean dry forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_dry_forests" title="Trinidad and Tobago dry forests">Trinidad and Tobago dry forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands_xeric_scrub" title="Windward Islands xeric scrub">Windward Islands xeric scrub</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_mangroves" title="Trinidad mangroves">Trinidad mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-110">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is noted particularly for its large number of bird species, and is a popular destination for <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">bird watchers</a>. Notable species include the <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_ibis" title="Scarlet ibis">scarlet ibis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rufous-vented_chachalaca" title="Rufous-vented chachalaca">cocrico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egret" title="Egret">egret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shiny_cowbird" title="Shiny cowbird">shiny cowbird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bananaquit" title="Bananaquit">bananaquit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oilbird" title="Oilbird">oilbird</a> and various species of <a href="/wiki/Honeycreeper" title="Honeycreeper">honeycreeper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trogon" title="Trogon">trogon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toucan" title="Toucan">toucan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parrot" title="Parrot">parrot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanager" title="Tanager">tanager</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodpecker" title="Woodpecker">woodpecker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antbird" title="Antbird">antbird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kite_(bird)" title="Kite (bird)">kites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawk" title="Hawk">hawks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Booby" title="Booby">boobies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pelican" title="Pelican">pelicans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vulture" title="Vulture">vultures</a>; there are also 17 species of hummingbird, including the <a href="/wiki/Tufted_coquette" title="Tufted coquette">tufted coquette</a> which is the world's third smallest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018274-275_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018274-275-111">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Information about invertebrates is dispersed and very incomplete. About 650 butterflies,<sup id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-106">[102]</a></sup> at least 672 beetles (from Tobago alone)<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[108]</a></sup> and 40 corals<sup id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-106">[102]</a></sup> have been recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_106-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-106">[102]</a></sup> Other notable invertebrates include the <a href="/wiki/Cockroach" title="Cockroach">cockroach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leafcutter_ant" title="Leafcutter ant">leaf-cutter ant</a> and numerous species of <a href="/wiki/Mosquito" title="Mosquito">mosquitoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Termite" title="Termite">termites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spider" title="Spider">spiders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarantula" title="Tarantula">tarantulas</a>. </p>
      <p>Although the list is far from complete, 1,647 species of fungi, including lichens, have been recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[111]</a></sup> The true total number of fungi is likely to be far higher, given the generally accepted estimate that only about 7% of all fungi worldwide have so far been discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[112]</a></sup> A first effort to estimate the number of endemic fungi tentatively listed 407 species.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Information about micro-organisms is dispersed and very incomplete. Nearly 200 species of marine algae have been recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_106-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-106">[102]</a></sup> The true total number of micro-organism species must be much higher. </p>
      <p>Thanks to a recently published checklist, plant diversity in Trinidad and Tobago is well documented with about 3,300 species (59 endemic) recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity_106-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Convention_on_Biological_Diversity-106">[102]</a></sup> Despite significant felling, forests still cover about 40% of the country, and there are about 350 different species of tree.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018270_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018270-104">[100]</a></sup> A notable tree is the <a href="/wiki/Manchineel" title="Manchineel">manchineel</a> which is extremely poisonous to humans, and even just touching its sap can cause severe blistering of the skin; the tree is often covered with warning signs. The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.62/10, ranking it 69th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-118">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Threats to the country's biodiversity include over-hunting and poaching (see <a href="/wiki/Hunting#Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Hunting">Hunting#Trinidad and Tobago</a>), habitat loss and fragmentation (particularly due to forest fires and land clearance for quarrying, agriculture, squatting, housing and industrial development and road construction), water pollution, and introduction of invasive species and pathogens. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

      </div>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is a republic with a <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">two-party system</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliamentary system based on the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster System">Westminster System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> of Trinidad and Tobago is the President, currently <a href="/wiki/Paula-Mae_Weekes" title="Paula-Mae Weekes">Paula-Mae Weekes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> This largely ceremonial role replaced that of the Governor-General (representing the <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Queen of Trinidad and Tobago">Monarch of Trinidad and Tobago</a>) upon Trinidad and Tobago's becoming a republic in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Trinidad and Tobago">Prime Minister</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Keith_Rowley" title="Keith Rowley">Keith Rowley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> The President is elected by an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_college" title="Electoral college">Electoral college</a> consisting of the full membership of both houses of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Parliament of Trinidad and Tobago">Parliament</a>. The Prime Minister is elected following a general election which takes place every five years. The President is required to appoint the leader of the party who in his or her opinion has the most support of the members of the House of Representatives to this post; this has generally been the leader of the party which won the most seats in the previous election (except in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_general_election,_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinidad and Tobago general election, 2001">2001 General Elections</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 1980 Tobago has also had its own elections, separate from the general elections. In these elections, members are elected and serve in the unicameral Tobago House of Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Parliament consists of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Trinidad and Tobago">Senate</a> (31 seats) and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Trinidad and Tobago">House of Representatives</a> (41 seats, plus the Speaker).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[116]</a></sup> The members of the Senate are appointed by the president; 16 Government Senators are appointed on the advice of the Prime Minister, six Opposition Senators are appointed on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Trinidad_and_Tobago)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Trinidad and Tobago)">Leader of the Opposition</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Kamla_Persad-Bissessar" title="Kamla Persad-Bissessar">Kamla Persad-Bissessar</a>, and nine Independent Senators are appointed by the President to represent other sectors of civil society. The 41 members of the House of Representatives are elected by the people for a maximum term of five years in a "<a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">first past the post</a>" system. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg/310px-Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg/465px-Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg/620px-Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="938"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Regional_corporations_and_municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Regional corporations and municipalities of Trinidad and Tobago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad is split into 14 <a href="/wiki/Regional_Corporations_and_Municipalities_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Corporations and Municipalities of Trinidad and Tobago">regional corporations and municipalities</a>, consisting of nine regions and five municipalities, which have a limited level of autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> The various councils are made up of a mixture of elected and appointed members. Elections are held every three years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The country was formerly divided into <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Counties of Trinidad and Tobago">counties</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The two main parties are the People's National Movement (PNM) and the United National Congress (UNC). Support for these parties appears to fall along ethnic lines, with the PNM consistently obtaining a majority of Afro-Trinidadian vote, and the UNC gaining a majority of Indo-Trinidadian support. Several smaller parties also exist. As of the August 2020 General Elections, there were 19 registered political parties. These include, the Progressive Empowerment Party, Trinidad Humanity Campaign, New National Vision, Movement for Social Justice, Congress of the People, Movement for National Development, Progressive Democratic Patriots, National Coalition for Transformation, Progressive Party, Independent Liberal Party, Democratic Party of Trinidad and Tobago, National Organisation of We the People, Unrepresented Peoples Party, Trinidad and Tobago Democratic Front, The National Party, One Tobago Voice, and Unity of the Peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Defence_Force" title="Trinidad and Tobago Defence Force">Trinidad and Tobago Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg/220px-T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg/330px-T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg/440px-T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1996" data-file-height="1315"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:T%26T_Port_of_Spain-1-tonal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Coast Guard vessel in action
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Trinidad and Tobago Defence Force (TTDF) is the military organisation responsible for the defence of the twin island Republic of Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Regiment" title="Trinidad and Tobago Regiment">Regiment</a>, the Coast Guard, the <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Force of Trinidad and Tobago">Air Guard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Defence_Force#Defence_Force_Reserves" title="Trinidad and Tobago Defence Force">Defence Force Reserves</a>. Established in 1962 after Trinidad and Tobago's independence from the United Kingdom, the TTDF is one of the largest military forces in the Anglophone Caribbean.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Its mission statement is to "defend the sovereign good of The Republic of Trinidad and Tobago, contribute to the development of the national community and support the State in the fulfilment of its national and international objectives". The Defence Force has been engaged in domestic incidents, such as the 1990 coup attempt, and international missions, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Mission in Haiti">United Nations Mission in Haiti</a> between 1993 and 1996. </p>
      <p>In 2019, Trinidad and Tobago signed the UN treaty on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Foreign relations of Trinidad and Tobago">Foreign relations of Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago maintains close relations with its <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> neighbours and major North American and European trading partners. As the most industrialised and second-largest country in the Anglophone Caribbean, Trinidad and Tobago has taken a leading role in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM), and strongly supports CARICOM economic integration efforts. It also is active in the <a href="/wiki/Summit_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Summit of the Americas">Summit of the Americas</a> process and supports the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Area_of_the_Americas" title="Free Trade Area of the Americas">Free Trade Area of the Americas</a>, lobbying other nations for seating the Secretariat in Port of Spain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>As a member of CARICOM, Trinidad and Tobago strongly backed efforts by the United States to bring political stability to <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, contributing personnel to the Multinational Force in 1994. After its 1962 independence, Trinidad and Tobago joined the United Nations and Commonwealth of Nations. In 1967 it became the first Commonwealth country to join the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS).<sup id="cite_ref-oas.org_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oas.org-123">[119]</a></sup> In 1995 Trinidad played host to the inaugural meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> and has become the seat of this 35-member grouping, which seeks to further economic progress and integration among its states. In international forums, Trinidad and Tobago has defined itself as having an independent voting record, but often supports US and EU positions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_crime">Law enforcement and crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Law enforcement and crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Crime in Trinidad and Tobago">Crime in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago has in recent decades suffered from a relatively high crime rate;<sup id="cite_ref-smartraveller1_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smartraveller1-124">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-125">[121]</a></sup> there are currently roughly 500 murders per year.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018256_83-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018256-83">[79]</a></sup> The country is a noted transshipment centre for the trafficking of illegal drugs from South America to the rest of the Caribbean and beyond to North America.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[123]</a></sup> Some estimates put the size of the "hidden economy" as high as 20–30% of measured GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terrorism">Terrorism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Terrorism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Though there have been no terrorism-related incidents in the country since the 1990 coup attempt, Trinidad and Tobago remains a potential target; for example, in February 2018 a plan to attack the Carnival was foiled by police.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-125">[121]</a></sup> It is estimated that roughly 100 citizens of the country have travelled to the Middle East to fight for <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-smartraveller1_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smartraveller1-124">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-125">[121]</a></sup> In 2017 the government adopted a counter-terrorism and extremism strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-125">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago_Prison_Service">Trinidad and Tobago Prison Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago Prison Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The country's prison administration is the Trinidad and Tobago Prison Service (TTPS), it is under the control of the Commissioner of Prisons (Ag.) Dennis Pulchan, located in Port-of-Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-prisonstudies.org_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prisonstudies.org-129">[125]</a></sup> The prison population rate is 292 people per 100,000. The total prison population, including pre-trial detainees and remand prisoners, is 3,999 prisoners. The population rate of pre-trial detainees and remand prisoners is 174 per 100,000 of the national population (59.7% of the prison population). In 2018, the female prison population rate is 8.5 per 100,000 of the national population (2.9% of the prison population). Prisoners that are minors makes up 1.9% of the prison population and foreigners prisoners make 0.8% of the prison population. The occupancy level of Trinidad and Tobago's prison system is at 81.8% capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-prisonstudies.org_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prisonstudies.org-129">[125]</a></sup> Trinidad and Tobago has nine prison establishments; Golden Grove Prison, Maximum Security Prison, Port of Spain Prison, Eastern Correctional Rehabilitation Centre, Remand Prison, Tobago Convict Prison, Carrera Convict Island Prison, Women's Prison and Youth Training and Rehabilitation Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[126]</a></sup> Trinidad and Tobago also use labour yards as prisons, or means of punishment.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[127]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Demographics of Trinidad and Tobago">Demographics of Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of the country currently stands at 1,363,985 (July 2019 est.).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The ethnic composition of Trinidad and Tobago reflects a history of conquest and immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[129]</a></sup> While the earliest inhabitants were of Amerindian heritage, the two dominant groups in the country are now those of South Asian and of African heritage. <a href="/wiki/Indo-Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian">Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonians</a> make up the country's largest ethnic group (approximately 35.4%);<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> they are primarily the descendants of indentured workers from <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> (mostly from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>), brought to replace freed African slaves who refused to continue working on the sugar plantations. Through cultural preservation many residents of Indian descent continue to maintain traditions from their ancestral homeland. Indo-Trinidadians reside primarily on Trinidad; as of the 2011 census only 2.5% of Tobago's population was of Indian descent.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-134">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Afro-Trinidadians_and_Tobagonians" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Trinidadians and Tobagonians">Afro-Trinidadians and Tobagonians</a> make up the country's second largest ethnic group, with approximately 34.2% of the population identifying as being of African descent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> The majority of people of an African background are the descendants of slaves forcibly transported to the islands from as early as the 16th century. This group constitute the majority on Tobago, at 85.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-134">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The bulk of the rest of the population are those who identify as being of mixed heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> There are also small but significant minorities of people of Amerindian, <a href="/wiki/White_Trinidadian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Trinidadian">European</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Chinese Trinidadian and Tobagonian">Chinese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> descent. <a href="/wiki/Arima" title="Arima">Arima</a> on Trinidad is a noted centre of Amerindian culture.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago#Language" title="Demographics of Trinidad and Tobago">Demographics of Trinidad and Tobago §&nbsp;Language</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="English_and_English_creoles">English and English creoles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: English and English creoles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian_English" title="Trinidadian and Tobagonian English">Trinidadian and Tobagonian English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidadian_Creole" title="Trinidadian Creole">Trinidadian Creole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tobagonian_Creole" title="Tobagonian Creole">Tobagonian Creole</a>
      </div> 
      <p>English is the country's official language (the local variety of standard English is <a href="/wiki/Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian_English" title="Trinidadian and Tobagonian English">Trinidadian and Tobagonian English</a> or more properly, Trinidad and Tobago Standard English, abbreviated as "TTSE"), but the main spoken language is either of two <a href="/wiki/English-based_creole_languages" title="English-based creole languages">English-based creole languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/Trinidadian_Creole" title="Trinidadian Creole">Trinidadian Creole</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tobagonian_Creole" title="Tobagonian Creole">Tobagonian Creole</a>), which reflects the Amerindian, European, African, and Asian heritage of the nation. Both creoles contain elements from a variety of African languages; Trinidadian English Creole, however, is also influenced by French and <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole_French" class="mw-redirect" title="Antillean Creole French">French Creole</a> (Patois).<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hindustani">Hindustani</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Hindustani">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani#Trinidadian_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Caribbean Hindustani §&nbsp;Trinidadian Hindustani</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The variant of Caribbean Hindustani that is spoken in Trinidad and Tobago is known as <i>Trinidadian Hindustani</i>, <i>Trinidadian Bhojpuri</i>, <i>Plantation Hindustani</i>, or <i>Gaon ke Bolee (Village Speech)</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-70">[66]</a></sup> A majority of the early Indian immigrants spoke <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Awadhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Awadhi">Awadhi</a>, which later formed into Trinidadian Hindustani. In 1935, Indian movies began showing to audiences in Trinidad. Most of the Indian movies were in the <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">Standard Hindustani (Hindi-Urdu) dialect</a> and this modified Trinidadian Hindustani slightly by adding Standard <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> phrases and vocabulary to Trinidadian Hindustani. Indian movies also revitalized Hindustani among Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonians.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[132]</a></sup> Around the mid to late 1970s the <i>lingua franca</i> of Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonians switched from Trinidadian Hindustani to a sort of "Hindinized" version of English. Today Hindustani survives on through <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean_music" title="Indo-Caribbean music">Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian musical forms</a> such as, <a href="/wiki/Bhajan" title="Bhajan">Bhajan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_folk_music" title="Indian folk music">Indian folk music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filmi" title="Filmi">Filmi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pichakaree" title="Pichakaree">Pichakaree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chutney_music" title="Chutney music">Chutney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chutney_soca" title="Chutney soca">Chutney soca</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chutney_parang" title="Chutney parang">Chutney parang</a>. As of 2003, there are about 15,633 Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonians who speak Trinidadian Hindustani and as of 2011, there are 10,000 who speak Standard Hindi. Many Indo-Trinidadians and Tobagonians today speak a type of <a href="/wiki/Hinglish" title="Hinglish">Hinglish</a> that consist of Trinidadian and Tobagonian English that is heavily laced with Trinidadian Hindustani vocabulary and phrases and many Indo-Trinidadians and Tobagonians can recite phrases or prayers in Hindustani today. There are many places in Trinidad and Tobago that have names of Hindustani origin. Some phrases and vocabulary have even made its way into the mainstream English and English Creole dialect of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-70">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[137]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindi_Day" title="Hindi Day">World Hindi Day</a> is celebrated each year with events organized by the National Council of Indian Culture, Hindi Nidhi Foundation, Indian High Commission, Mahatma Gandhi Institute, and the <a href="/wiki/Sanatan_Dharma_Maha_Sabha" title="Sanatan Dharma Maha Sabha">Sanatan Dharma Maha Sabha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup> Attempts to preserve Trinidadian Hindustani are being made by Caribbean Hindustani Inc. led by Visham Bhimull.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish">Spanish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Spanish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Spanish language in Trinidad and Tobago">Spanish language in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt">
         In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish language</a> was the native language of 4,000 people (or 0.3&nbsp;% of the total population) living in Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup> The number has grown substantially thanks to the massive immigration of Venezuelans due to the crisis that the country has been suffering in the last decade.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other local languages are <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinidad and Tobago English">English</a> (official) and other unofficial languages such as <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Caribbean Hindustani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">French Creole</a> and others.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tamil">Tamil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tamil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil language</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tamil_diaspora#Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Tamil diaspora">Tamil diaspora §&nbsp;Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Tamil language is spoken by some of the older <a href="/wiki/Tamils" title="Tamils">Tamil (Madrasi)</a> Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian population. It is mostly spoken by the few remaining children of indentured Indian labourers from the present-day state of <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Other speakers of the language are recent immigrants from Tamil Nadu.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[141]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese">Chinese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Chinese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese language</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Chinese language first came to Trinidad and Tobago in 1806, when the British had brought Chinese labourers in order to determine if they were fit to use as labourers after the abolition of slavery.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> About 2,645 Chinese immigrants arrived in Trinidad as indentured labour between 1853 and 1866.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A majority of the people who immigrated in the 19th century were from <a href="/wiki/South_China" title="South China">southern China</a> and spoke the <a href="/wiki/Hakka_Chinese" title="Hakka Chinese">Hakka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yue_Chinese" title="Yue Chinese">Yue</a> dialects of Chinese. In the 20th century after the years of indentureship up to the present-day more Chinese people have immigrated to Trinidad and Tobago for business and they speak the dialects of the indenturees along with other Chinese dialects, such as <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Min_Chinese" title="Min Chinese">Min</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-studycountry.com_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-studycountry.com-146">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[143]</a></sup> J. Dyer Ball, writing in 1906, says: "In Trinidad there were, about twenty years ago, 4,000 or 5,000 Chinese, but they have decreased to probably about 2,000 or 3,000, [2,200 in 1900]. They used to work in sugar plantations, but are now principally shopkeepers, as well as general merchants, miners and railway builders, etc."<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_languages">Indigenous languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Indigenous languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The indigenous languages were Yao on Trinidad and <a href="/wiki/Karina_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Karina language">Karina</a> on Tobago, both Cariban, and <a href="/wiki/Shebaya_language" title="Shebaya language">Shebaya</a> on Trinidad, which was Arawakan.<sup id="cite_ref-studycountry.com_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-studycountry.com-146">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Religion in Trinidad and Tobago">Religion in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Hinduism in Trinidad and Tobago">Hinduism in Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Islam in Trinidad and Tobago">Islam in Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Orisha" title="Trinidad Orisha">Trinidad Orisha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist" title="Spiritual Baptist">Spiritual Baptist</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg/150px-TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg/225px-TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg/300px-TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TnT_Hanuman_Statue_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 26-meter <a href="/wiki/Hanuman" title="Hanuman">Hanuman</a> murti in <a href="/wiki/Carapichaima" title="Carapichaima">Carapichaima</a>, a noted centre of Hindu and Indo-Trinidadian culture; it is the largest statue of Hanuman outside of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2011 census,<sup id="cite_ref-2011Census_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Census-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> were the largest single religious group in Trinidad and Tobago with 21.60% of the total population. The <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>/<a href="/wiki/Evangelical" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a>/<a href="/wiki/Full_Gospel" title="Full Gospel">Full Gospel</a> denominations were the third largest group with 12.02% of the population. The remaining population is made of various Christian denominations (<a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist" title="Spiritual Baptist">Spiritual</a> <a href="/wiki/Shouter_Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Shouter Baptist">Shouter</a> <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> (5.67%), <a href="/wiki/Anglicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a> (5.67%), <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> (4.09%), <a href="/wiki/Presbyterians" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterians">Presbyterians</a> or <a href="/wiki/Congregationalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregationalists">Congregationalists</a> (2.49%), <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (1.47%), other Baptists (1.21%), <a href="/wiki/Methodists" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> (0.65%) and the <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravian Church</a> (0.27%)). Respondents who did not state a religious affiliation represented 11.1% of the population, with 2.18% declaring themselves <a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">Irreligious</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> were the second largest group with 18.15%.<sup id="cite_ref-2011Census_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Census-3">[3]</a></sup> Hinduism is practised throughout the country and <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a> is a public holiday, and other <a href="/wiki/Hindu_holidays" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu holidays">Hindu holidays</a> are also widely celebrated. The largest Hindu organization in Trinidad and Tobago is the <a href="/wiki/Sanatan_Dharma_Maha_Sabha" title="Sanatan Dharma Maha Sabha">Sanatan Dharma Maha Sabha</a>, which was formed in 1952 after the merging of the two main Hindu organizations. Most Hindus in Trinidad and Tobago are <a href="/wiki/San%C4%81tan%C4%AB" title="Sanātanī">Sanātanī (Sanatanist/Orthodox Hindu)</a>. Other sects and organizations include the <a href="/wiki/Arya_Samaj" title="Arya Samaj">Arya Samaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kabir_panth" title="Kabir panth">Kabir Panth</a>, Seunariani (Sieunarini/Shiv Narayani), <a href="/wiki/Ramanandi_Sampradaya" title="Ramanandi Sampradaya">Ramanandi Sampradaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aghor_Yoga" title="Aghor Yoga">Aughar (Aghor)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ravidassia_religion" title="Ravidassia religion">Ravidas Panth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kali" title="Kali">Kali Mai (Madrasi)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sathya_Sai_Baba_movement" title="Sathya Sai Baba movement">Sathya Sai Baba movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirdi_Sai_Baba_movement" title="Shirdi Sai Baba movement">Shirdi Sai Baba movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Society_for_Krishna_Consciousness" title="International Society for Krishna Consciousness">ISKCON (Hare Krishna)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinmaya_Mission" title="Chinmaya Mission">Chinmaya Mission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Sevashram_Sangha" title="Bharat Sevashram Sangha">Bharat Sevashram Sangha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Divine_Life_Society" title="Divine Life Society">Divine Life Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaumaram" title="Kaumaram">Murugan (Kaumaram)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ganapathi_Sachchidananda" title="Ganapathi Sachchidananda">Ganapathi Sachchidananda movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jagadguru_Kripalu_Parishat" title="Jagadguru Kripalu Parishat">Jagadguru Kripalu Parishat (Radha Madhav)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brahma_Kumaris" title="Brahma Kumaris">Brahma Kumaris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> represent 4.97% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-2011Census_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Census-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a> is a public holiday and <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Mawlid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hosay" title="Hosay">Hosay</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Islamic_holidays" title="Islamic holidays">Muslim holidays</a> are also celebrated. There has also been a Jewish community on the islands for many centuries, however their numbers have never been large, with a 2007 estimating putting the Jewish population at 55 individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-Luxner2007_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luxner2007-151">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Siegel2015_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Siegel2015-152">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>African-derived or Afrocentric religions are also practised, notably <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Orisha" title="Trinidad Orisha">Trinidad Orisha</a> (<a href="/wiki/Yoruba_religion" title="Yoruba religion">Yoruba</a>) believers (0.9%) and <a href="/wiki/Rastafarians" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafarians">Rastafarians</a> (0.27%).<sup id="cite_ref-2011Census_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Census-3">[3]</a></sup> Various aspects of traditional <a href="/wiki/Obeah" title="Obeah">obeah</a> beliefs are still commonly practised on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018251_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERough_Guides2018251-56">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:200px; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Trinidad and Tobago (2011 census)<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[149]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">Percent</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Christianity</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:blue; width:55.5%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">55.5%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:#F4C430; width:20.4%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">20.4%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:5.6%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5.6%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"> None/not shared</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:grey; width:2.5%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.5%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Two <a href="/wiki/African_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="African culture">African</a> <a href="/wiki/Syncretic" class="mw-redirect" title="Syncretic">syncretic</a> faiths, the Shouter or <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist" title="Spiritual Baptist">Spiritual Baptists</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Orisha" title="Trinidad Orisha">Orisha</a> faith (formerly called <a href="/wiki/Shango" title="Shango">Shangos</a>, a less than complimentary term)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> are among the fastest growing religious groups. Similarly, there is a noticeable increase in numbers of <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Protestant">Evangelical Protestant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fundamentalist_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundamentalist Christian">Fundamentalist</a> churches usually lumped as "<a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>" by most Trinidadians, although this designation is often inaccurate. <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> are practised by a minority of <a href="/wiki/Indo-Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian">Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonians</a>. Several eastern religions such as <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> are followed by a minority of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Chinese Trinidadian and Tobagonian">Chinese Trinidadian and Tobagonian</a>, with most being Christians. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Urban centres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Education in Trinidad and Tobago">Education in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
