      <p> Children generally start pre-school at two and a half years but this is not mandatory. They are however, expected to have basic reading and writing skills when they commence primary school. Students proceed to a primary school at the age of five years. Seven years are spent in primary school. The seven classes of primary school consists of First Year and Second Year, followed by Standard One through Standard Five. During the final year of primary school, students prepare for and sit the Secondary Entrance Assessment (SEA) which determines the secondary school the child will attend.</p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg/220px-TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg/330px-TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg/440px-TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TnT_St._Augustine_UWI_Campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Augustine,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Saint Augustine, Trinidad and Tobago">St. Augustine</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Students attend secondary school for a minimum of five years, leading to the CSEC (Caribbean Secondary Education Certificate) examinations, which is the equivalent of the British GCSE O levels. Children with satisfactory grades may opt to continue high school for a further two-year period, leading to the Caribbean Advanced Proficiency Examinations (CAPE), the equivalent of GCE A levels. Both CSEC and CAPE examinations are held by the Caribbean Examinations Council (CXC). Public Primary and Secondary education is free for all, although private and religious schooling is available for a fee. </p>
      <p>Tertiary education for tuition costs are provided for via GATE (The Government Assistance for Tuition Expenses), up to the level of the bachelor's degree, at the University of the West Indies (UWI), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="University of Trinidad and Tobago">University of Trinidad and Tobago</a> (UTT), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Southern_Caribbean" title="University of the Southern Caribbean">University of the Southern Caribbean</a> (USC), the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Science,_Technology_and_Applied_Arts_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="College of Science, Technology and Applied Arts of Trinidad and Tobago">College of Science, Technology and Applied Arts of Trinidad and Tobago</a> (COSTAATT) and certain other local accredited institutions. Government also currently subsidises some Masters programmes. Both the Government and the private sector also provide financial assistance in the form of academic scholarships to gifted or needy students for study at local, regional or international universities. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Women in Trinidad and Tobago">Women in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>While women account for only 49% of the population, they constitute nearly 55% of the workforce in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Economy of Trinidad and Tobago">Economy of Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="751"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_and_Tobago_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Trinidad and Tobago's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Refinerypointeapierre.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Refinerypointeapierre.JPG/220px-Refinerypointeapierre.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Refinerypointeapierre.JPG/330px-Refinerypointeapierre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Refinerypointeapierre.JPG/440px-Refinerypointeapierre.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Refinerypointeapierre.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The oil refinery at <a href="/wiki/Pointe-%C3%A0-Pierre" title="Pointe-à-Pierre">Pointe-à-Pierre</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is the most developed nation and one of the wealthiest in the Caribbean and is listed in the top 40 (2010 information) of the 70 <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">high-income countries</a> in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Its gross national income per capita of US$20,070<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[154]</a></sup> (2014 gross national income at Atlas Method) is one of the highest in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[155]</a></sup> In November 2011, the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> removed Trinidad and Tobago from its list of <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[156]</a></sup> Trinidad's economy is strongly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> industry. Tourism and manufacturing are also important to the local economy. Tourism is a growing sector, particular on Tobago, although proportionately it is much less important than in many other Caribbean islands. Agricultural products include citrus and cocoa. It also supplies manufactured goods, notably food, beverages, and cement, to the Caribbean region. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_gas">Oil and gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Oil and gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is the leading Caribbean producer of oil and gas, and its economy is heavily dependent upon these resources.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> Oil and gas account for about 40% of GDP and 80% of exports, but only 5% of employment.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> Recent growth has been fuelled by investments in liquefied natural gas (LNG), petrochemicals, and steel. Additional petrochemical, aluminium, and plastics projects are in various stages of planning. </p>
      <p>The country is also a regional financial centre, and the economy has a growing trade surplus.<sup id="cite_ref-back_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-back-99">[95]</a></sup> The expansion of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_LNG" title="Atlantic LNG">Atlantic LNG</a> over the past six years created the largest single-sustained phase of economic growth in Trinidad and Tobago. The nation is an exporter of LNG and supplied a total of 13.4&nbsp;billion m<sup>3</sup> in 2017. The largest markets for Trinidad and Tobago's LNG exports are Chile and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-161">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago has transitioned from an oil-based economy to a natural gas based economy. In 2017, natural gas production totalled 18.5&nbsp;billion m<sup>3</sup>, a decrease of 0.4% from 2016 with 18.6&nbsp;billion m<sup>3</sup> of production.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-161">[157]</a></sup> Oil production has decreased over the past decade from 7.1&nbsp;million metric tonnes per year in 2007 to 4.4&nbsp;million metric tonnes per year in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[158]</a></sup> In December 2005, the Atlantic LNG's fourth production module or "train" for liquefied natural gas (LNG) began production. Train four has increased Atlantic LNG's overall output capacity by almost 50% and is the largest LNG train in the world at 5.2&nbsp;million tons/year of LNG.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg/220px-Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg/330px-Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg/440px-Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pigeon_Point_beach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tourists at <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_Point,_Tobago" title="Pigeon Point, Tobago">Pigeon Point</a> beach, Tobago
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is far less dependent on tourism than many other Caribbean countries and territories, with the bulk of tourist activity occurring on Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> The government has made efforts to boost this sector in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Historically agricultural production (for example, sugar and coffee) dominated the economy, however this sector has been in steep decline since the 20th century and now forms just 0.4% of the country's GDP, employing 3.1% of the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> Various fruits and vegetables are grown, such as cucumbers, eggplant, cassava, pumpkin, dasheen (taro) and coconut; fishing is still also commonly practised.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_diversification">Economic diversification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Economic diversification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago, in an effort to undergo economic transformation through diversification,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago_19-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_-_Trinidad_and_Tobago-19">[15]</a></sup> formed <a href="/wiki/InvesTT" title="InvesTT">InvesTT</a> in 2012 to serve as the country's sole investment promotion agency. This agency is aligned to the Ministry of Trade and Industry and is to be the key agent in growing the country's non-oil and gas sectors significantly and sustainably.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications_infrastructure">Communications infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Communications infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago has a well developed communications sector. The telecommunications and broadcasting sectors generated an estimated TT$5.63&nbsp;billion (US$0.88&nbsp;billion) in 2014, which as a percentage of GDP equates to 3.1 percent. This represented a 1.9 percent increase in total revenues generated by this industry compared to last year. Of total telecommunications and broadcasting revenues, mobile voice services accounted for the majority of revenues with TT$2.20&nbsp;billion (39.2 percent). This was followed by internet services which contributed TT$1.18&nbsp;billion or 21.1 percent. The next highest revenue earners for the industry were fixed voice services and paid television services whose contributions totalled TT$0.76&nbsp;billion and TT$0.70&nbsp;billion respectively (13.4 percent and 12.4 percent). International voice services was next in line, generating TT$0.27&nbsp;billion (4.7 percent) in revenues. Free-to Air radio and television services contributed TT$0.18&nbsp;billion and TT$0.13&nbsp;billion respectively (3.2 percent and 2.4 percent). Finally, other contributors included "other revenues" and "leased line services" with earnings of TT$0.16&nbsp;billion and TT$0.05&nbsp;billion respectively, with 2.8 percent and 0.9 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are several providers for each segment of the telecommunications market. Fixed Lines Telephone service is provided by <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a>, <a href="/wiki/TSTT" class="mw-redirect" title="TSTT">TSTT</a> (operating as <a href="/wiki/Bmobile" title="Bmobile">bmobile</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Cable_%26_Wireless_Communications" title="Cable &amp; Wireless Communications">Cable &amp; Wireless Communications</a> operating as <a href="/wiki/Flow_(brand)" title="Flow (brand)">FLOW</a>; cellular service is provided by <a href="/wiki/TSTT" class="mw-redirect" title="TSTT">TSTT</a> (operating as bmobile) and Digicel whilst internet service is provided by <a href="/wiki/TSTT" class="mw-redirect" title="TSTT">TSTT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flow_(brand)" title="Flow (brand)">FLOW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a>, Green Dot and Lisa Communications. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_industries">Creative industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Creative industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Government of Trinidad and Tobago has recognised the creative industries as a pathway to economic growth and development. It is one of the newest, most dynamic sectors where creativity, knowledge and intangibles serve as the basic productive resource. In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Creative_Industries_Company" title="Trinidad and Tobago Creative Industries Company">Trinidad and Tobago Creative Industries Company</a> Limited (CreativeTT) was established as a state agency under the Ministry of Trade and Industry with a mandate to stimulate and facilitate the business development and export activities of the Creative Industries in Trinidad and Tobago to generate national wealth, and, as such, the company is responsible for the strategic and business development of the three (3) niche areas and sub sectors currently under its purview – <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Music of Trinidad and Tobago">Music</a>, Film and Fashion. <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Music_Company" title="Trinidad and Tobago Music Company">MusicTT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Film_Company" title="Trinidad and Tobago Film Company">FilmTT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Fashion_Company" title="Trinidad and Tobago Fashion Company">FashionTT</a> are the subsidiaries established to fulfil this mandate. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Transport in Trinidad and Tobago">Transport in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CRHUBH_intersection.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/CRHUBH_intersection.JPG/220px-CRHUBH_intersection.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/CRHUBH_intersection.JPG/330px-CRHUBH_intersection.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/CRHUBH_intersection.JPG/440px-CRHUBH_intersection.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="1296"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CRHUBH_intersection.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An intersection of <a href="/wiki/Churchill%E2%80%93Roosevelt_Highway" title="Churchill–Roosevelt Highway">Churchill–Roosevelt Highway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uriah_Butler_Highway" title="Uriah Butler Highway">Uriah Butler Highway</a>, 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The transport system in Trinidad and Tobago consists of a dense network of highways and roads across both major islands, ferries connecting Port of Spain with Scarborough and <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="San Fernando, Trinidad and Tobago">San Fernando</a>, and international airports on both islands.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Uriah_Butler_Highway" title="Uriah Butler Highway">Uriah Butler Highway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Roosevelt_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Churchill Roosevelt Highway">Churchill Roosevelt Highway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Solomon_Hochoy_Highway" title="Sir Solomon Hochoy Highway">Sir Solomon Hochoy Highway</a> links the island of Trinidad together, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Claude_Noel_Highway" title="Claude Noel Highway">Claude Noel Highway</a> is the only major highway in Tobago. Public transportation options on land are public buses, private taxis and minibuses. By sea, the options are inter-island ferries and inter-city water taxis.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The island of Trinidad is served by <a href="/wiki/Piarco_International_Airport" title="Piarco International Airport">Piarco International Airport</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Piarco" title="Piarco">Piarco</a>, which opened on 8 January 1931.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Elevated at 17.4 metres (57&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a> it comprises an area of 680 hectares (1,700 acres) and has a runway of 3,200 metres (10,500&nbsp;ft). The airport consists of two terminals, the North Terminal and the South Terminal. The older South Terminal underwent renovations in 2009 for use as a VIP entrance point during the 5th Summit of the Americas. The North Terminal was completed in 2001, and consists of<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[162]</a></sup> 14-second-level aircraft gates with jetways for international flights, two ground-level domestic gates and 82 ticket counter positions. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_(8504733249).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_%288504733249%29.jpg/220px-Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_%288504733249%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_%288504733249%29.jpg/330px-Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_%288504733249%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_%288504733249%29.jpg/440px-Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_%288504733249%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3013" data-file-height="2007"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_Airlines_Boeing_737-800_9Y-TAB_(8504733249).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Airlines" title="Caribbean Airlines">Caribbean Airlines</a> is the largest in the region.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2008 the passenger throughput at Piarco International Airport was approximately 2.6&nbsp;million. It is the seventh busiest airport in the Caribbean and the third busiest in the English-speaking Caribbean, after <a href="/wiki/Sangster_International_Airport" title="Sangster International Airport">Sangster International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lynden_Pindling_International_Airport" title="Lynden Pindling International Airport">Lynden Pindling International Airport</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Caribbean Airlines, the national airline, operates its main hub at the Piarco International Airport and services the Caribbean, the United States, Canada and South America. The airline is wholly owned by the Government of Trinidad and Tobago. After an additional cash injection of US$50&nbsp;million, the Trinidad and Tobago government acquired the Jamaican airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Jamaica" title="Air Jamaica">Air Jamaica</a> on 1 May 2010, with a 6–12-month transition period to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Island of Tobago is served by the <a href="/wiki/A.N.R._Robinson_International_Airport" title="A.N.R. Robinson International Airport">A.N.R. Robinson International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Crown_Point,_Tobago" title="Crown Point, Tobago">Crown Point</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> This airport has regular services to North America and Europe. There are regular flights between the two islands, with fares being heavily subsidised by the Government. </p>
      <p>Trinidad was formerly home to a <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Government_Railway" title="Trinidad Government Railway">railway network</a>, however this was closed down in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[164]</a></sup> There have been talks to build a new railway on the islands, though nothing yet has come of this.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_policy_and_climate">Energy policy and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Energy policy and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is the region's leading exporter of oil and gas but imports of fossil fuels provided over 90% of the energy consumed by its CARICOM neighbours in 2008. This vulnerability led CARICOM to develop an Energy Policy which was approved in 2013. This policy is accompanied by the CARICOM Sustainable Energy Roadmap and Strategy (C-SERMS). Under the policy, renewable energy sources are to contribute 20% of the total electricity generation mix in member states by 2017, 28% by 2022 and 47% by 2027.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-170">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014 Trinidad and Tobago was the third country in the world which emitted the most <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> per capita after <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curacao" class="mw-redirect" title="Curacao">Curacao</a> according to the World Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-test_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-171">[167]</a></sup> On average, each inhabitant produced 34.2 metric tons of <span class="nowrap"><span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br>2</span></span></span> in the atmosphere. In comparison, the world average was 5.0 tons per capita the same year. </p>
      <p>The Caribbean Industrial Research Institute in Trinidad and Tobago facilitates climate change research and provides industrial support for R&amp;D related to food security. It also carries out equipment testing and calibration for major industries.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-170">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Culture of Trinidad and Tobago">Culture of Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg/220px-Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg/330px-Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg/440px-Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Orange_Carnival_Masqueraders_in_Trinidad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Masqueraders during <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Carnival" title="Trinidad and Tobago Carnival">Carnival</a> celebrations
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Divalinagar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Divalinagar.jpg/220px-Divalinagar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Divalinagar.jpg/330px-Divalinagar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Divalinagar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="332" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Divalinagar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Divali_Nagar" title="Divali Nagar">Divali Nagar</a> entrance in <a href="/wiki/Chaguanas" title="Chaguanas">Chaguanas</a>; Divali Nagar is one of the largest Diwali celebration outside <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[169]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago has a diverse culture mixing Indian, African, Creole, Chinese, Amerindian, Arab, Latino, and European influences, reflecting the various communities who have migrated to the islands over the centuries. The island is particularly renowned for its annual <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Carnival" title="Trinidad and Tobago Carnival">Carnival</a> celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-EBTT_20-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBTT-20">[16]</a></sup> Festivals rooted in various religions and cultures practised on the islands are also popular, such as <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, Independence Day, Republic Day, <a href="/wiki/Divali" class="mw-redirect" title="Divali">Divali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Arrival_Day" title="Indian Arrival Day">Indian Arrival Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phagwah" class="mw-redirect" title="Phagwah">Phagwah (Holi)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navaratri" title="Navaratri">Nauratri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vijayadashami" title="Vijayadashami">Dussehra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maha_Shivaratri" title="Maha Shivaratri">Maha Shivratri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmashtami" title="Krishna Janmashtami">Krishna Janmashtami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rama_Navami" title="Rama Navami">Ram Naumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanuman_Jayanti" title="Hanuman Jayanti">Hanuman Jayanti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ganesh_Utsav" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganesh Utsav">Ganesh Utsav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Day" title="Emancipation Day">Emancipation Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_Baptist/Shouter_Liberation_Day" title="Spiritual Baptist/Shouter Liberation Day">Spiritual Baptist/Shouter Liberation Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">Maundy Thursday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Year%E2%80%99s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="New Year’s Day">New Year’s Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_Corpus_Christi" title="Feast of Corpus Christi">Feast of Corpus Christi</a>, <a href="/wiki/All_Souls%27_Day" title="All Souls' Day">All Souls' Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints' Day">All Saints' Day</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[170]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hosay" title="Hosay">Hosay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Mawlid</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa_First_Peoples_Community" title="Santa Rosa First Peoples Community">Santa Rosa Indigenous Festival</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_literature" title="Trinidad and Tobago literature">Trinidad and Tobago literature</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago claims two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize</a>-winning authors, <a href="/wiki/V._S._Naipaul" title="V. S. Naipaul">V. S. Naipaul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">St Lucian</a>-born <a href="/wiki/Derek_Walcott" title="Derek Walcott">Derek Walcott</a> (who also founded the Trinidad Theatre Workshop). Other notable writers include <a href="/wiki/Neil_Bissoondath" title="Neil Bissoondath">Neil Bissoondath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vahni_Capildeo" title="Vahni Capildeo">Vahni Capildeo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earl_Lovelace" title="Earl Lovelace">Earl Lovelace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seepersad_Naipaul" title="Seepersad Naipaul">Seepersad Naipaul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shiva_Naipaul" title="Shiva Naipaul">Shiva Naipaul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Persaud" title="Lakshmi Persaud">Lakshmi Persaud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Ramchand" title="Kenneth Ramchand">Kenneth Ramchand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Rampersad" title="Arnold Rampersad">Arnold Rampersad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Selvon" class="mw-redirect" title="Samuel Selvon">Samuel Selvon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Maharaj" title="Rabindranath Maharaj">Rabindranath Maharaj</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_design">Art and design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Art and design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago_artists" title="List of Trinidad and Tobago artists">List of Trinidad and Tobago artists</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidadian designer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Minshall" title="Peter Minshall">Peter Minshall</a> is renowned not only for his Carnival costumes but also for his role in opening ceremonies of the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">Barcelona Olympics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1996_Summer_Olympics" title="1996 Summer Olympics">1996 Summer Olympics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympics</a>, for which he won an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[171]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Music of Trinidad and Tobago">Music of Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Theaterspektakel_(2010)_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG/220px-Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG/330px-Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG/440px-Theaterspektakel_%282010%29_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Theaterspektakel_(2010)_2010-09-04_19-02-50.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">Steelpan</a> was invented in Trinidad.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg/220px-Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg/330px-Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg/440px-Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3664" data-file-height="2748"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Trinidad_and_Tobago_Sweet_Tassa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tassa" title="Tassa">Tassa</a> is a popular percussion ensemble of Indian origin that is popular in Trinidad and Tobago.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">steelpan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[174]</a></sup> Trinidad is also the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chutney_music" title="Chutney music">chutney music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chutney-soca" class="mw-redirect" title="Chutney-soca">chutney-soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parang" title="Parang">parang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rapso" title="Rapso">rapso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pichakaree" title="Pichakaree">pichakaree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chutney_parang" title="Chutney parang">chutney parang</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Limbo_(dance)" title="Limbo (dance)">limbo</a> dance originated in Trinidad as an event that took place at <a href="/wiki/Wake_(ceremony)" title="Wake (ceremony)">wakes</a> in Trinidad. The limbo has African roots. It was popularized in the 1950s by dance pioneer <a href="/wiki/Julia_Edwards_(dancer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Julia Edwards (dancer)">Julia Edwards</a><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[175]</a></sup> (known as the "First Lady of Limbo") and her company which appeared in several films.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[176]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Bélé">Bélé</a>, Bongo, and whining are also dance forms with African roots.<sup id="cite_ref-discovertnt.com_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discovertnt.com-181">[177]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jazz_dance" title="Jazz dance">Jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ballroom_dance" title="Ballroom dance">ballroom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">modern</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_(dance)" title="Salsa (dance)">salsa</a> dancing are also popular.<sup id="cite_ref-discovertnt.com_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discovertnt.com-181">[177]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Dance_in_India" title="Dance in India">Indian dance forms</a> are also prevalent in Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[178]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kathak" title="Kathak">Kathak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odissi" title="Odissi">Odissi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bharatanatyam" title="Bharatanatyam">Bharatanatyam</a> are the most popular <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_dance" title="Indian classical dance">Indian classical dance forms</a> in Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-academia.edu_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia.edu-183">[179]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_folk_dances" title="List of Indian folk dances">Indian folk dances</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_dance" class="mw-redirect" title="Bollywood dance">Bollywood dances</a> are also popular.<sup id="cite_ref-academia.edu_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academia.edu-183">[179]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago_films" title="List of Trinidad and Tobago films">List of Trinidad and Tobago films</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_cuisine" title="Trinidad and Tobago cuisine">Trinidad and Tobago cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Holder" title="Geoffrey Holder">Geoffrey Holder</a> (brother of <a href="/wiki/Boscoe_Holder" title="Boscoe Holder">Boscoe Holder</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Heather_Headley" title="Heather Headley">Heather Headley</a> are two Trinidad-born artists who have won <a href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a> for theatre. Holder also has a distinguished film career, and Headley has won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> as well. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_India" title="Theatre of India">Indian theatre</a> is also popular throughout Trinidad and Tobago. <a href="/wiki/Nautanki" title="Nautanki">Nautankis</a> and dramas such as <i><a href="/wiki/Harischandra" class="mw-redirect" title="Harischandra">Raja Harishchandra</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Shravan" title="Shravan">Sharwan Kumar</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Alha-Khand" title="Alha-Khand">Alha-Khand</a></i> were brought by Indians to Trinidad and Tobago, however they had largely began to die out, till preservation began by Indian cultural groups.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[180]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Ramlila" title="Ramlila">Ramleela</a></i>, the drama about the life of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> deity <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Rama</a>, is popular during the time between <a href="/wiki/Navaratri" title="Navaratri">Sharad Navaratri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dushera" class="mw-redirect" title="Dushera">Dushera</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Rasa_Lila" class="mw-redirect" title="Rasa Lila">Ras leela (Krishna leela)</a></i>, the drama about the life of the Hindu deity <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>, is popular around the time of <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmashtami" title="Krishna Janmashtami">Krishna Janmashtami</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Trinidad and Tobago is also smallest country to have two Miss Universe titleholders and the first <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">black</a> woman ever to win: <a href="/wiki/Janelle_Commissiong" title="Janelle Commissiong">Janelle Commissiong</a> in 1977, followed by <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Fitzwilliam" title="Wendy Fitzwilliam">Wendy Fitzwilliam</a> in 1998; the country has also had one Miss World titleholder, <a href="/wiki/Giselle_LaRonde" class="mw-redirect" title="Giselle LaRonde">Giselle LaRonde</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_sports">Olympic sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Olympic sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_at_the_Olympics" title="Trinidad and Tobago at the Olympics">Trinidad and Tobago at the Olympics</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hasely_Crawford" title="Hasely Crawford">Hasely Crawford</a> won the first Olympic <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">gold medal</a> for Trinidad and Tobago in the men's <a href="/wiki/100_metre_dash" class="mw-redirect" title="100 metre dash">100-metre dash</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Summer Olympics</a>. Nine different athletes from Trinidad and Tobago have won twelve medals at the Olympics, beginning with a <a href="/wiki/Silver_medal" title="Silver medal">silver medal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a>, won by Rodney Wilkes in <a href="/wiki/1948_Summer_Olympics" title="1948 Summer Olympics">1948</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[184]</a></sup> and most recently, a gold medal by <a href="/wiki/Keshorn_Walcott" title="Keshorn Walcott">Keshorn Walcott</a> in the men's <a href="/wiki/Javelin_throw" title="Javelin throw">javelin throw</a> in <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ato_Boldon" title="Ato Boldon">Ato Boldon</a> has won the most Olympic and World Championship medals for Trinidad and Tobago in athletics, with eight in total – four from the Olympics and four from the World Championships. Boldon was the sole world champion Trinidad and Tobago has produced until <a href="/wiki/Jehue_Gordon" title="Jehue Gordon">Jehue Gordon</a> in <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2013 World Championships in Athletics">Moscow 2013</a>. Ato won the 1997 <a href="/wiki/200_meters" class="mw-redirect" title="200 meters">200&nbsp;m sprint</a> World Championship in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. Swimmer <a href="/wiki/George_Bovell" title="George Bovell">George Bovell</a> III won a bronze medal in the men's <a href="/wiki/200_metres_Individual_Medley" class="mw-redirect" title="200 metres Individual Medley">200 m IM</a> in 2004. At the 2017 World Championship in London, the Men 4x400 relay team captured the title, thus the country now celebrates three world championships titles. The team consisted of <a href="/wiki/Jarrin_Solomon" title="Jarrin Solomon">Jarrin Solomon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jareem_Richards" class="mw-redirect" title="Jareem Richards">Jareem Richards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machel_Cedenio" title="Machel Cedenio">Machel Cedenio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lalonde_Gordon" title="Lalonde Gordon">Lalonde Gordon</a> with <a href="/wiki/Renny_Quow" title="Renny Quow">Renny Quow</a> who ran in the heats. </p>
      <p>Also in 2012 <a href="/wiki/Lalonde_Gordon" title="Lalonde Gordon">Lalonde Gordon</a> competed in the XXX Summer Olympics where he won a bronze medal in the 400 metres (1,300 feet), being surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Luguelin_Santos" class="mw-redirect" title="Luguelin Santos">Luguelin Santos</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kirani_James" title="Kirani James">Kirani James</a> of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>. Keshorn Walcott (as stated above) came first in javelin and earned a gold medal, making him the second Trinidadian in the country's history to receive one. This also makes him the first Western<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> athlete in 40 years to receive a gold medal in the javelin sport, and the first athlete from Trinidad and Tobago to win a gold medal in a field event in the Olympics. Sprinter Richard Thompson is also from Trinidad and Tobago. He came second place to Usain Bolt in the Beijing Olympics in the 100 metres (330 feet) with a time of 9.89s. </p>
      <p>In 2018 The Court of Arbitration for Sport made its final decision on the failed doping sample from the Jamaican team in the 4 x 100 relay in the 2008 Olympic Games. The team from Trinidad and Tobago will be awarded the gold medal, because of the second rank during the relay run.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[185]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_cricket_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national cricket team">Trinidad and Tobago national cricket team</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg/220px-BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg/330px-BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg/440px-BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1440"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BrianLaraUkexpat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Brian_Lara" title="Brian Lara">Brian Lara</a> batting for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a> against <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">India</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Cricket is a popular sport of Trinidad and Tobago, often deemed the national sport, and there is intense inter-island rivalry with its Caribbean neighbours. Trinidad and Tobago is represented at <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="Twenty20 cricket">Twenty20 cricket</a> level as a member of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies team</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinidad and Tobago cricket team">national team</a> plays at the <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class</a> level in regional competitions such as the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Four_Day_Competition" title="Regional Four Day Competition">Regional Four Day Competition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_Super50" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Super50">Regional Super50</a>. Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Trinbago_Knight_Riders" title="Trinbago Knight Riders">Trinbago Knight Riders</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Premier_League" title="Caribbean Premier League">Caribbean Premier League</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_Oval" title="Queen's Park Oval">Queen's Park Oval</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a> is the largest cricket ground in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, having hosted 60 Test matches as of January 2018. Trinidad and Tobago along with other islands from the Caribbean co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Brian_Lara" title="Brian Lara">Brian Lara</a>, world record holder for the most runs scored both in a Test and in a First Class innings and other records, was born in a small town of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Santa Cruz, Trinidad and Tobago">Santa Cruz</a> and is often referred to as the Prince of Port of Spain or simply the Prince. This legendary West Indian batsman is widely regarded. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Association_football_in_Trinidad_and_Tobago" class="mw-redirect" title="Association football in Trinidad and Tobago">Association football in Trinidad and Tobago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Association football is also a popular sport in Trinidad and Tobago. <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">The men's national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> for the first time by beating <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_national_football_team" title="Bahrain national football team">Bahrain</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manama" title="Manama">Manama</a> on 16 November 2005, making them the second smallest country ever (in terms of population) to qualify, after <a href="/wiki/Iceland_national_football_team" title="Iceland national football team">Iceland</a>. The team, coached by <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutchman</a> <a href="/wiki/Leo_Beenhakker" title="Leo Beenhakker">Leo Beenhakker</a>, and led by Tobagonian-born captain <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Yorke" title="Dwight Yorke">Dwight Yorke</a>, drew their first group game – against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, 0–0, but lost the second game to <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> on late goals, 0–2. They were eliminated after losing 2–0 to <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a> in the last game of the Group stage. Prior to the 2006 World Cup qualification, Trinidad and Tobago came close in a controversial qualification campaign for the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a>. Following the match, the referee of their critical game against <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> was awarded a lifetime ban for his actions.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[186]</a></sup> Trinidad and Tobago again fell just short of qualifying for the World Cup in <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a>, needing only a draw at home against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a> but losing 1–0.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[187]</a></sup> They play their home matches at the <a href="/wiki/Hasely_Crawford_Stadium" title="Hasely Crawford Stadium">Hasely Crawford Stadium</a>. Trinidad and Tobago hosted the <a href="/wiki/2001_FIFA_U-17_World_Championship" title="2001 FIFA U-17 World Championship">2001 FIFA U-17 World Championship</a>, and hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup">2010 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/TT_Pro_League" title="TT Pro League">TT Pro League</a> is the country's primary football competition and is the top level of the <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_football_league_system" title="Trinidad and Tobago football league system">Trinidad and Tobago football league system</a>. The Pro League serves as a league for professional football clubs in Trinidad and Tobago. The league began in 1999 as part of a need for a professional league to strengthen the country's <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">national team</a> and improve the development of domestic players. The first season took place in the same year beginning with eight teams. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trinidad_and_Tobago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
